makeDataRequest(ctx context.Context, lokiDsUrl string, query lokiQuery) (*http.Request, error) {\n\tqs := url.Values{}\n\tqs.Set(\"query\", query.Expr)\n\n\tqs.Set(\"direction\", string(query.Direction))\n\n\t// MaxLines defaults to zero when not received,\n\t// and Loki does not like limit=0, even when it is not needed\n\t// (for example for metric queries), so we\n\t// only send it when it's set\n\tif query.MaxLines > 0 {\n\t\tqs.Set(\"limit\", fmt.Sprintf(\"%d\", query.MaxLines))\n\t}\n\n\tlokiUrl, err := url.Parse(lokiDsUrl)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, strconv.FormatInt(query.Start.UnixNano(), 10))\n\t\t\tqs.Set(\"end\", strconv.FormatInt(query.End.UnixNano(), 10))\n\t\t\t// NOTE: technically for streams-producing queries `step`\n\t\t\t// is ignored, so it would be nicer to not send it in such cases,\n\t\t\t// but we cannot detect that situation, so we always send it.\n\t\t\t// it should not break anything.\n\t\t\t// NOTE2: we do this at millisecond precision for two reasons:\n\t\t\t//  a. Loki cannot do steps with better precision anyway,\n\t\t\t//     so the microsecond & nanosecond part can be ignored.\n\t\t\t//  b. having it always be number+'ms' makes it more robust and\n\t\t\t//     precise, as Loki does not support step with float number\n\t\t\t//     and time-specifier, like \"1.5s\"\n\t\t\tqs.Set(\"step\", fmt.Sprintf(\"%dms\", query.Step.Milliseconds()))\n\t\t\tlokiUrl.Path makeLokiError(bytes []byte) error {\n\tvar data lokiError\n\terr := json.Unmarshal(bytes, &data)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\t// we were unable to convert the bytes to JSON, we return the whole text\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"%v\", string(bytes))\n\t}\n\n\tif data.Message == \"\" {\n\t\t// we got no usable error message, we return the whole text\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"%v\", string(bytes))\n\t}\n\n\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"%v\", data.Message)\n}\n\n// we know there is an error,\n// based on the http-response-body\n// we have to make an informative error-object\nfunc readLokiError(body io.ReadCloser) error {\n\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n\t_, err := buf.ReadFrom(body)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tbytes := buf.Bytes()\n\n\t// the error-message is probably a JSON structure,\n\t// with a string-field named \"message\". we want the\n\t// value of that field.\n\t// but, the response might be just a simple string,\n\t// this was used in older Loki versions.\n\t// so our approach is this:\n\t// - we try to convert the bytes to JSON\n\t// - we take the value of the field \"message\"\n\t// - if any of these steps fail, or if \"message\" is empty, we return the whole text\n\n\treturn makeLokiError(bytes)\n}\n\nfunc (api *LokiAPI) DataQuery(ctx context.Context, query lokiQuery, responseOpts ResponseOpts) (*backend.DataResponse, error) {\n\treq, have to make an informative error-object\n   139→func readLokiError(body io.ReadCloser) error {\n   140→\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n   141→\t_, err := buf.ReadFrom(body)\n   142→\tif err != nil {\n   143→\t\treturn err\n   144→\t}\n   145→\n   146→\tbytes := buf.Bytes()\n   147→\n   148→\t// the error-message is probably a JSON structure,\n   149→\t// with a string-field named \"message\". we want the\n   150→\t// value of that field.\n   151→\t// but, the response might be just a simple string,\n   152→\t// this was used in older Loki versions.\n   153→\t// so our approach is this:\n   154→\t// - we try to convert the bytes to JSON\n   155→\t// - we take the value of the field \"message\"\n   156→\t// - if any of these steps fail, or if \"message\" is empty, we return the whole text\n   157→\n   158→\treturn makeLokiError(bytes)\n   159→}\n   160→\n   161→func (api *LokiAPI) DataQuery(ctx context.Context, query lokiQuery, responseOpts ResponseOpts) (*backend.DataResponse, getSupportingQueryHeaderValue(supportingQueryType SupportingQueryType) string {\n   322→\tvalue := \"\"\n   323→\n   324→\t// we need to map the SupportingQueryType to the actual header value. For\n   325→\t// legacy reasons we defined each value, such as \"logsVolume\" maps to the\n   326→\t// \"logvolhist\" header value to Loki. With #85123, even the value set in the\n   327→\t// frontend query can be passed as is to Loki.\n   328→\tswitch supportingQueryType {\n   329→\tcase SupportingQueryLogsVolume:\n   330→\t\tvalue = \"logvolhist\"\n   331→\tcase SupportingQueryLogsSample:\n   332→\t\tvalue = \"logsample\"\n   333→\tcase SupportingQueryDataSample:\n   334→\t\tvalue = \"datasample\"\n   335→\tcase SupportingQueryInfiniteScroll:\n   336→\t\tvalue = \"infinitescroll\"\n   337→\tdefault:\n   338→\t\tvalue = string(supportingQueryType)\n   339→\t}\n   340→\n   341→\treturn value\n   342→}\n   343→\n   344→// setXScopeOrgIDHeader sets the `X-Scope-OrgID` header in the provided HTTP request based on the tenant ID retrieved from the context.\n   345→// `X-Scope-OrgID` is needed by the Loki system to work in multi-tenant mode.\n   346→// See https://github.com/grafana/loki/blob/main/docs/sources/operations/multi-tenancy.md\n   347→func setXScopeOrgIDHeader(req *http.Request, ctx context.Context) *http.Request {\n   348→\tlogger := backend.NewLoggerWith(\"logger\", \"tsdb.loki\")\n   349→\n   350→\tmd, ok := metadata.FromIncomingContext(ctx)\n   351→\tif !ok {\n   352→\t\t// Metadata are currently set and needed only locally for multi-tenancy, while on cloud\n   353→\t\t// this is set by our stack\n   354→\t\tlogger.Debug(\"Metadata not present in context. Header not set\")\n   355→\t\treturn req\n   356→\t}\n   357→\n   358→\ttenantids := md.Get(\"tenantid\")\n   359→\tif len(tenantids) == 0 {\n   360→\t\t// We assume we are not using multi-tenant mode, which is fine\n   361→\t\tlogger.Debug(\"Tenant ID not present. Header not set\")\n   362→\t} else if len(tenantids) > 1 {\n   363→\t\t// Loki supports multiple tenant IDs, but we should receive them from different contexts\n   364→\t\tlogger.Error(strconv.Itoa(len(tenantids)) + \" tenant IDs found. Header not set\")\n   365→\t} else {\n   366→\t\treq.Header.Add(\"X-Scope-OrgID\", tenantids[0])\n   367→\t\tlogger.Debug(\"Tenant ID \" + tenantids[0] + \" added to Loki request\")\n   368→\t}\n   369→\treturn req\n   370→}\n   371→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. the\n   150→\t// value of that field.\n   151→\t// but, the response might be just a simple string,\n   152→\t// this was used in older Loki versions.\n   153→\t// so our approach is this:\n   154→\t// - we try to convert the bytes to JSON\n   155→\t// - we take the value of the field \"message\"\n   156→\t// - if any of these steps fail, or if \"message\" is empty, we return the whole text\n   157→\n   158→\treturn makeLokiError(bytes)\n   159→}\n   160→\n   161→func (api *LokiAPI) DataQuery(ctx context.Context, query lokiQuery, responseOpts ResponseOpts) (*backend.DataResponse,
